Inherent vs. Dispositional Possibility
The commentator responds to an objection by distinguishing inherent and dispositional possibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between inherent possibility (imkan dhati) and dispositional possibility (imkan isti'dadi) and why this distinction is crucial for arguments about the existence of a locus for possibility.

Core Idea
Possibility is of two kinds: one conceptual and invariant, the other real and varying.

This passage addresses a key objection: if possibility is a conceptual matter, how can it require an existing locus? The commentator responds by clarifying that there are two distinct types of possibility. Inherent possibility is a conceptual attribute inseparable from essence, while dispositional possibility is a real quality that subsists in a locus. This distinction resolves the objection and refines the foundation of arguments for creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and the answer
Start by reading the passage's objection that possibility, being conceptual, does not need a locus. Then note how the commentator answers by distinguishing two types of possibility.
Pay attention to the phrase 'we say' (قلنا) which marks the answer.
2
Identify the two types of possibility
The commentator defines inherent possibility (al-imkan al-dhati) as conceptual, necessary for essence, and invariant. Dispositional possibility (al-imkan al-isti'dadi) is a real quality (kayf) that subsists in a locus and varies in strength.
Inherent possibility is inseparable from essence; dispositional possibility is subject to change.
3
Understand the implications for the argument
The objection was based on inherent possibility, but the argument for a locus uses dispositional possibility. This shows why the argument stands.
The commentator clarifies that the previous arguments refer to dispositional possibility.
4
Examine the glosses on conceptual matters
The glosses explain that conceptual matters do require a locus in the mind, and that possibility is positive (thubuti) not negative. This reinforces the need for a subject in the mind.
The commentator emphasizes that possibility is a capacity, not a mere negation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإمكان أمر اعتباري كما سبق وأنتم معترفون به. والأمور الاعتبارية لا تستدعي محلاً موجوداً، فكيف تستدلون بثبوت الإمكان قبل وجود الحادث على محل موجود يقوم به إمكانه . ( قلنا : المراد بهذا الإمكان ) الذي يستدل به على وجود محله ( هو الإمكان الاستعدادي، وأنه غير الإمكان الذاتي؛ لأن الإمكان الذاتي أمر اعتباري يعقل للشيء عند انتساب ماهيته إلى الوجود وهو لازم لماهية الممكن قائم بها، يستحيل انفكاكه عنها، كما مر ولا يتصور فيه تفاوت بالقوة والضعف، والقرب والبعد أصلاً، بخلاف الإمكان الاستعدادي فإنه أمر موجود من مقولة الكيف، قائم بمحل الشيء الذي ينسب إليه الإمكان لا به، وغيره لازم له وقابل للتفاوت . ثم إن ظاهر عبارتهم الاستدلال بالإمكان الذاتي، فأراد توضيح المرام فقال : ( وتحقيقه ) أي تحقيق الإمكان الاستعدادي. قوله : (يوهم الاستدلال ) أي يدل دلالة ظاهرة على هذه المقدمة الوهمية الكاذبة، لا أن الاستدلال يوهم . قوله : ( والأمور الاعتبارية لا تستدعي محلاً موجوداً أي موجوداً في الخارج، كما هو هاهنا، وأما استدعاؤها محلاً موجوداً في الجملة، ولو في الذهن، فقاعدة أن ثبوت شيء لشيء فرع ثبوت المثبت له تقتضيه ثم الظاهر أن مفهوم الإمكان ثبوتي، وهو قابلية الوجود والعدم، لا سلبي كما يشعر به تفسيرهم إياه بسلب الضرورة، إذ لو كان سلبياً لكان قولنا : الحادث ممكن موجبة سالبة المحمول غير مقتض لوجود الموضوع، فكان الممتنع حال عدمه في الذهن ممكناً، لاتصافه بهذا السلب لا ،ممتنعاً لأن اقتضاء العدم أمر ثبوتي يستدعي وجود الموضوع في الجملة؛ وهو باطل قطعاً، ولكون السلب المذكور لازماً لهذا المعنى الوجودي يعبر عنه به، فالحادث لا يتصف بالإمكان الذاتي قبل وجوده في الخارج وفي الذهن، كما لا يتصف بالامتناع حتى يلزم الانقلاب وأما إذا وجد في الذهن فيتصف به، ويقوم به إمكانه، فلا يلزم وجود أمر في الخارج يقوم به الإمكان الذاتي للحادث هذا. ويمكن الجدل في اتصاف الممتنع قبل وجوده في الذهن بالإمكان ولو كان أمراً سلبياً، بأن عدم ثبوت الممتنع في المبادئ العالية الكافي في اتصافه في الامتناع أمر محال، جاز أن يستلزم محالاً آخر، أعني عدم اتصافه بضرورة أحد الطرفين، وبسلبه أيضا، قليتأمل . قوله : ( ثم إن ظاهر عبارتهم إلخ) خصوصاً قولهم الإمكان وجودي؛ لما مر من أدلة وجوده، وقد عرفت توجيهه
Possibility (al-imkan) is a conceptual matter (amr i'tibari) as previously and you acknowledge it. And conceptual matters do not require an existing locus. So how do you infer from the establishment of possibility before the existence of the temporal being to an existing locus that sustains its possibility? (We say: what is meant by this possibility) by which the existence of its locus is inferred (is dispositional possibility (al-imkan al-isti'dadi), and it is other than inherent possibility (al-imkan al-dhati); because inherent possibility is a conceptual matter that is understood for the thing when its essence (mahiyya) is related to existence, and it is necessary for the essence of the possible subsisting in it, impossible to separate from it, as has passed, and no variation in it by strength and weakness, nearness and distance is conceivable at all, unlike dispositional possibility, for it is an existing thing from the category of quality (kayf), subsisting in the locus of the thing to which possibility is attributed, not in it, and other than it is necessary for it and it is subject to variation. Then the apparent meaning of their expression is inference by inherent possibility, so he intended to clarify the intended meaning and said: (and its verification) i.e., the verification of dispositional possibility. His saying: (it suggests the inference) i.e., it indicates a clear indication of this false illusory premise, not that the inference is illusory. His saying: (and conceptual matters do not require an existing locus) i.e., existing in the external world, as is the case here. As for their requiring a locus existing in some sense, even if in the mind, the rule that the existence of a thing for another is a branch of the existence of the subject for it necessitates it. Then the apparent meaning is that the concept of possibility is positive (thubuti), and it is the capacity for existence and non-existence, not negative as their interpretation of it by the negation of necessity would suggest. For if it were negative, our saying 'the temporal being is possible' would be an affirmative proposition with a negative predicate not requiring the existence of the subject, so the impossible at the time of its non-existence in the mind would be possible because it is described by this negation, not impossible, because the requirement of non-existence is a positive matter that requires the existence of the subject in some sense; and that is absolutely false. And because the mentioned negation is necessary for this positive meaning, it is expressed by it. So the temporal being is not described by inherent possibility before its existence in the external world and in the mind, just as it is not described by impossibility so that reversal would occur. But if it exists in the mind, it is described by it, and its possibility subsists in it, so there does not follow the existence of something in the external world that sustains the inherent possibility of the temporal being. This. And one could argue about the impossible being described before its existence in the mind by possibility, even if it were a negative matter, by saying that the non-existence of the impossible in the high principles sufficient for its being described as impossibility is an impossible matter, so it may necessitate another impossible, namely its not being described by the necessity of one of the two sides, and also by its negation. Let it be considered. His saying: (then the apparent meaning of their expression etc.) especially their saying 'possibility is existential' because of what has passed of the proofs of its existence, and you have understood its interpretation.
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and its answer, followed by clarifying glosses. The objector argues that possibility is a conceptual matter (amr i'tibari) and therefore does not require a real locus, challenging the previous argument for matter. The answer distinguishes between two types of possibility: inherent (dhati) and dispositional (isti'dadi). Inherent possibility is a conceptual attribute inseparable from the essence, invariant, and does not require a substratum. Dispositional possibility is a real quality (kayf) that subsists in a locus and is subject to variation. The commentator notes that the previous argument was about dispositional possibility, not inherent. The subsequent glosses explain that the phrase 'suggests the inference' warning against a false premise, and clarify that conceptual matters do require a locus in the mind, but not necessarily in the external world. Further, possibility (imkan) is a positive concept (capacity for both existence and non-existence) rather than a simple negation, and the commentator discusses implications for the description of the temporal being before its existence. The final gloss emphasizes that the author's expression aligns with the existential nature of possibility. This passage refines the understanding of possibility fundamental to arguments for creation.

Key Terms
imkan dhati (inherent possibility)
imkan isti'dadi (dispositional possibility)
amr i'tibari (conceptual matter)
kayf (quality)
mahall (locus)
thubuti (positive/ existential)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that all possibility is of the same kind and that if possibility is conceptual, it cannot require any locus at all.
Correction: The passage clarifies that there are two kinds: inherent possibility (conceptual, no external locus needed) and dispositional possibility (real, requires a locus). The argument for a locus uses dispositional possibility, not inherent.

Checkpoint
What is the key difference between inherent possibility (al-imkan al-dhati) and dispositional possibility (al-imkan al-isti'dadi) according to this passage?
A) Inherent possibility is real while dispositional is conceptual
B) Inherent possibility is necessary for the essence and does not vary, while dispositional possibility is a real quality that varies and requires a locus
C) Inherent possibility requires a locus while dispositional does not
D) Both are conceptual and require no locus

Key Takeaway
Inherent possibility is conceptual and invariable, while dispositional possibility is real, varying, and requires a locus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You often think about possibilities in your life—what you could become. But is your possibility inherent (fixed by your essence) or dispositional (changeable through effort)? How does this distinction from the lesson change how you view your potential for spiritual growth? What must you do today to turn your inherent potential into real readiness?
?
The objector assumed possibility doesn't require a locus. But you may assume your good intentions are enough without physical practice. Where in your life have you mistaken conceptual possibility for real capacity? What will you do to ensure your faith has a 'locus' in action?
?
Possibility in this lesson is not a mere lack of necessity but a positive capacity. In your relationship with Allah, do you treat your ability to obey as a passive state or as a real quality that needs a substrate of consistent effort? What specific habit will you change starting today?

The Necessity of a Specific Subject for Successive Events
Main argument that successive events need a specific subject.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why a collection of successive events requires a specific subject, and how the argument avoids arbitrary preference (tarjih bila murajjih).

Core Idea
Without a specific subject, the choice of one event over another would be arbitrary.

This lesson presents the core argument that a series of successive events cannot exist without a specific material subject. The proof rests on the principle that without such specificity, the occurrence of one event rather than another would be an unjustified preference. We will see how this leads to the concept of successive dispositions.

Guided Path
1
Read the core proof passage
Read the Arabic passage carefully. It begins with the claim that the collection needs a specific subject, then gives the proof by reductio, and concludes about dispositions.
Focus on the logical flow: if no subject, then tarjih bila murajjih.
2
Understand the tarjih argument
The key point: without a specific subject, the relation of the collection to any event is equal, so specifying one event is arbitrary. This is a classical kalam argument.
3
Trace the conclusion about dispositions
The passage concludes that the subject must have successive dispositions, each preceding another without end. This sets up the need for an infinite chain of conditions.
This shows the argument is part of a larger metaphysical framework.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
له أي لذلك المجموع من محل يختص به أي بالحادث المفروض أولاً. ( وإلا ) وإن لم يتعلق ذلك المجموع بمحل كذلك، كان اختصاصه أي اختصاص مجموع الحوادث ( بحادث دون حادث آخر ترجيحاً بلا مرجح، فإنه إذا لم يتعلق المجموع بمحل أصلاً. أو تعلق بمحل لا اختصاص له بحادث معين كان نسبته إلى حادث معين كنسبته إلى غيره، فلم يكن حدوث أحدهما من المبدأ بتوسط ذلك المجموع أولى من حدوث غيره ،به فإذن (له أي لذلك المحل (استعدادات متعاقبة، كل واحد منها مسبوق بآخر لا إلى نهاية وكل (سابق) من تلك الاستعدادات ( شرط للاحق) أولاً، وحدوث ما فوق الشرط الأخير بواسطة حدوث مافوقه بواحد، وهلم جراً، وسيجيء تحقيق هذا البحث إن شاء الله تعالى .
قوله : ( فإنه إذا لم يتعلق إلخ) هذا بناء على ما قالوا من أن نسبة المباين إلى جميع الأشياء على السوية، لكنه مبحوث فيه : إذ يجوز أن يكون لتلك الشروط من حيث ذواتها اختصاص بذلك الحادث، وإن لم يكن في محل، أو كانت في محل لا اختصاص له بذلك الحادث.
قوله : (فإذن له إلخ) فإن قلت بعد ما ثبت أن لتلك الحوادث محلاً يختص بالحادث. ثبت أن الحادث مسبوق بالمادة، فلا حاجة إلى هذه المقدمات . قلت : لا نسلم ذلك؛ لأن ذلك المحل يجوز أن تكون ماهية ذلك الحادث متصفة به قبل وجوده فلا بد من إثبات أن تلك الشروط استعدادات متصفة بالقرب والبعد والشدة والضعف فتكون موجودة، فلا بد لها من محل موجود قبل وجود الحادث، فلا يكون محلها ماهيته . لوجودات الشروط وليس كذلك. وسيذكر الشارح في بحث إبطال التسلسل ما يندفع به هذا الكلام.
قوله : ( ولا بد له أي لذلك المجموع من محل يختص به قيل عليه : لو ثبت أنه لا بد لذلك المجموع من محل مختص بالحادث المفروض أولاً على أحد الأنحاء المذكورة في المباحث المشرقية، لتم مطلوبهم بلا حاجة إلى سائر المقدمات ولا يكون الاستدلال أيضاً بالإمكان الاستعدادي. والجواب : أن ثبوت المحل للمجموع على أحد الأنحاء المذكورة إنما يكون بسائر المقدمات المتضمنة للاستدلال بالإمكان الاستعدادي؛ إذ الثابت بدونها أن له محلاً، وأما أن ذلك المحل موجود كذا إما كذا وإما كذا فبسائر المقدمات؛ فتأمل .
قوله كنسبته إلى غيره فيه منع؛ لأن تلك الأمور المتعاقبة على تقدير تسليم جوازها ولزومها يجوز أن تكون أموراً قائمة بأنفسها مناسبة للحادث بحسب ذواتها على مراتب متفاوتة.
قوله : (أي لذلك المحل استعدادات فإن قلت: لم لم يعتبر في جانب الفاعل إمكان استعدادي بالنسبة إلى الفعل والإيجاد ؟ قلت لأن التفاوت ليس في الفاعلية؛ إذ الشرائط شرائط وجود المعلول ابتداء، وإن أمكن أن تعتبر بالعرض بالنسبة إلى الفاعل .
It [i.e., that collection] requires a subject that is specific to it, i.e., to the assumed first temporal event. (Otherwise) If that collection is not connected to a subject in such a way, then its specification—i.e., the specification of the collection of events—to one event rather than another would be a preference without a preponderant. For if the collection is not connected to any subject at all, or is connected to a subject that has no specificity to a particular event, then its relation to a particular event is like its relation to another, so the occurrence of one of them from the principle by means of that collection would not be more fitting than the occurrence of another by it. Therefore, that subject has successive dispositions, each of which is preceded by another without end, and every preceding disposition is a condition for the subsequent one, and the occurrence of what is above the last condition by means of the occurrence of what is above it by one, and so on. And the verification of this investigation will come, God willing.
His statement: "For if it is not connected, etc." This is based on what they said: that the relation of the separate [entity] to all things is equal, but it is debatable, for it is possible that those conditions, in terms of their essences, have a specificity to that event, even if not in a subject, or if they are in a subject that has no specificity to that event.
His statement: "Therefore, it has, etc." If you say: Once it is established that those events have a subject specific to the event, it is established that the event is preceded by matter, so there is no need for these premises. I say: We do not grant that; because that subject may be the essence of that event characterized prior to its existence, so it is necessary to prove that those conditions are dispositions characterized by proximity and distance, intensity and weakness, and thus they are existent, so they require an existent subject prior to the existence of the event, so their subject is not its essence. [This is] for the existences of the conditions, and it is not so. The commentator will mention in the investigation of refuting infinite regress what will refute this speech.
His statement: "And it [i.e., that collection] requires a subject specific to it." It was objected to him: If it were established that that collection requires a subject specific to the assumed first event in one of the ways mentioned in the Eastern investigations, their purpose would be achieved without need for the other premises, and the argument would also not be by dispositional potentiality. The answer: That the establishment of the subject for the collection in one of the mentioned ways is only through the other premises that include the argument by dispositional potentiality; for what is established without them is that it has a subject, but as for that subject being existent in such-and-such a way, it is through the other premises; so reflect.
His statement: "like its relation to another" — there is a denial; because those successive things, on the supposition of granting their permissibility and necessity, may be things subsisting by themselves, suitable for the event according to their essences in varying degrees.
His statement: "i.e., for that subject there are dispositions" — if you say: Why was not consideration given to the agent side of dispositional potentiality regarding the act and bringing into existence? I say: Because the variation is not in the agency; for the conditions are conditions of the existence of the effect initially, although they may be considered accidentally in relation to the agent.
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage provides the proof that a collection of successive events (e.g., a series of events leading to a temporal thing) must have a specific material subject (mahall). The author argues that without such a subject, the specification of one event over another would be an unjustified preference (tarjih bila murajjih). He then concludes that the subject must have successive dispositions (isti'dadat muta'aqiba), each preceding another ad infinitum. The passage then presents several objections and answers: 1) An objection that the argument assumes that a separate entity relates equally to all things, but the objector says the conditions could have inherent specificity. 2) An objection that once a subject is posited, the event is preceded by matter so no further premises are needed; the answer explains that the subject may be the quiddity of the event itself, so we need to prove that the conditions are existent dispositions requiring an existent subject. 3) An objection that if the necessity of a subject is granted, the argument is complete without needing dispositional potentiality; the answer clarifies that the necessity of a specific existing subject (not just any subject) requires the further premises. 4) An objection that the successive things could be self-subsistent entities suitable to the event; this is denied. 5) An objection asking why not consider dispositional potentiality in the agent; the answer says variation is in the effect, not in the agent's power. The argument thus defends the need for a material subject and successive dispositions.

Key Terms
محل
ترجيح بلا مرجح
استعدادات متعاقبة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that any subject, even a general one, is sufficient for the collection of events.
Correction: The passage shows that a general subject would make the relation equal to all events, leading to arbitrary selection, which is invalid. Only a specific subject avoids this.

Checkpoint
What is the main reason given in this passage for why a collection of successive events must have a specific subject?
A) Because otherwise the events would be impossible to exist.
B) Because otherwise the specification of one event over another would be arbitrary (preference without a preponderant).
C) Because the events are identical in essence.
D) Because the subject must be eternal.

Key Takeaway
A collection of successive events requires a specific subject; otherwise, the occurrence of any particular event would be arbitrary.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The argument shows that without a specific reason, events would be arbitrary. Think about a moment in your life when you assumed something happened by chance. Did that assumption weaken your conviction that every event is under Allah's wise control? How can you train yourself to see the 'specific subject'—the wisdom and cause—behind what seems random?
?
The passage says every preceding disposition is a condition for the next. In your journey of faith, what 'dispositions' have you been neglecting? Is there a spiritual condition you have left unmet—like sincere repentance, patience, or gratitude—that is preventing the next stage of growth? Commit to one specific disposition you will work on today.
?
If the specification of events to a particular subject is necessary to avoid arbitrariness, then consider your own choices: are they grounded in real causes and reasons, or do you sometimes act without reflection, merely following whim? What would it mean for your life to have every decision be 'specified' by a deliberate, God-conscious intention?

Objections and Answers to the Proof
Series of objections and their refutations defending the main proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key objections raised against the proof for a specific subject and how the author defends his position.

Core Idea
The proof is defended by showing that dispositions are existent and require a pre-existing subject.

After establishing that successive events need a specific subject with successive dispositions, several objections arise. This lesson examines those objections, including the possibility that the conditions themselves have inherent specificity, or that the subject could be the quiddity of the event. The author's responses clarify the necessity of the argument.

Guided Path
1
Review the first objection about equal relation
Read the objection that if conditions can have inherent specificity, the argument fails. The author responds that this is debatable.
Note the mention of 'المباحث المشرقية' (Eastern investigations) as an alternative view.
2
Examine the objection about the subject being the quiddity
This objection says that if the subject is the quiddity of the event itself, then the event is preceded by matter. The author responds that we need to prove the conditions are existent dispositions.
3
Understand the remaining objections and responses
The passage also addresses objections about the necessity of other premises, the possibility of self-subsistent conditions, and the role of the agent. Notice how each response reinforces the need for an existent subject.
The author often says 'فيه منع' or 'لا نسلم' to deny the objection's premise.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
له أي لذلك المجموع من محل يختص به أي بالحادث المفروض أولاً. ( وإلا ) وإن لم يتعلق ذلك المجموع بمحل كذلك، كان اختصاصه أي اختصاص مجموع الحوادث ( بحادث دون حادث آخر ترجيحاً بلا مرجح، فإنه إذا لم يتعلق المجموع بمحل أصلاً. أو تعلق بمحل لا اختصاص له بحادث معين كان نسبته إلى حادث معين كنسبته إلى غيره، فلم يكن حدوث أحدهما من المبدأ بتوسط ذلك المجموع أولى من حدوث غيره ،به فإذن (له أي لذلك المحل (استعدادات متعاقبة، كل واحد منها مسبوق بآخر لا إلى نهاية وكل (سابق) من تلك الاستعدادات ( شرط للاحق) أولاً، وحدوث ما فوق الشرط الأخير بواسطة حدوث مافوقه بواحد، وهلم جراً، وسيجيء تحقيق هذا البحث إن شاء الله تعالى .
قوله : ( فإنه إذا لم يتعلق إلخ) هذا بناء على ما قالوا من أن نسبة المباين إلى جميع الأشياء على السوية، لكنه مبحوث فيه : إذ يجوز أن يكون لتلك الشروط من حيث ذواتها اختصاص بذلك الحادث، وإن لم يكن في محل، أو كانت في محل لا اختصاص له بذلك الحادث.
قوله : (فإذن له إلخ) فإن قلت بعد ما ثبت أن لتلك الحوادث محلاً يختص بالحادث. ثبت أن الحادث مسبوق بالمادة، فلا حاجة إلى هذه المقدمات . قلت : لا نسلم ذلك؛ لأن ذلك المحل يجوز أن تكون ماهية ذلك الحادث متصفة به قبل وجوده فلا بد من إثبات أن تلك الشروط استعدادات متصفة بالقرب والبعد والشدة والضعف فتكون موجودة، فلا بد لها من محل موجود قبل وجود الحادث، فلا يكون محلها ماهيته . لوجودات الشروط وليس كذلك. وسيذكر الشارح في بحث إبطال التسلسل ما يندفع به هذا الكلام.
قوله : ( ولا بد له أي لذلك المجموع من محل يختص به قيل عليه : لو ثبت أنه لا بد لذلك المجموع من محل مختص بالحادث المفروض أولاً على أحد الأنحاء المذكورة في المباحث المشرقية، لتم مطلوبهم بلا حاجة إلى سائر المقدمات ولا يكون الاستدلال أيضاً بالإمكان الاستعدادي. والجواب : أن ثبوت المحل للمجموع على أحد الأنحاء المذكورة إنما يكون بسائر المقدمات المتضمنة للاستدلال بالإمكان الاستعدادي؛ إذ الثابت بدونها أن له محلاً، وأما أن ذلك المحل موجود كذا إما كذا وإما كذا فبسائر المقدمات؛ فتأمل .
قوله كنسبته إلى غيره فيه منع؛ لأن تلك الأمور المتعاقبة على تقدير تسليم جوازها ولزومها يجوز أن تكون أموراً قائمة بأنفسها مناسبة للحادث بحسب ذواتها على مراتب متفاوتة.
قوله : (أي لذلك المحل استعدادات فإن قلت: لم لم يعتبر في جانب الفاعل إمكان استعدادي بالنسبة إلى الفعل والإيجاد ؟ قلت لأن التفاوت ليس في الفاعلية؛ إذ الشرائط شرائط وجود المعلول ابتداء، وإن أمكن أن تعتبر بالعرض بالنسبة إلى الفاعل .
It [i.e., that collection] requires a subject that is specific to it, i.e., to the assumed first temporal event. (Otherwise) If that collection is not connected to a subject in such a way, then its specification—i.e., the specification of the collection of events—to one event rather than another would be a preference without a preponderant. For if the collection is not connected to any subject at all, or is connected to a subject that has no specificity to a particular event, then its relation to a particular event is like its relation to another, so the occurrence of one of them from the principle by means of that collection would not be more fitting than the occurrence of another by it. Therefore, that subject has successive dispositions, each of which is preceded by another without end, and every preceding disposition is a condition for the subsequent one, and the occurrence of what is above the last condition by means of the occurrence of what is above it by one, and so on. And the verification of this investigation will come, God willing.
His statement: "For if it is not connected, etc." This is based on what they said: that the relation of the separate [entity] to all things is equal, but it is debatable, for it is possible that those conditions, in terms of their essences, have a specificity to that event, even if not in a subject, or if they are in a subject that has no specificity to that event.
His statement: "Therefore, it has, etc." If you say: Once it is established that those events have a subject specific to the event, it is established that the event is preceded by matter, so there is no need for these premises. I say: We do not grant that; because that subject may be the essence of that event characterized prior to its existence, so it is necessary to prove that those conditions are dispositions characterized by proximity and distance, intensity and weakness, and thus they are existent, so they require an existent subject prior to the existence of the event, so their subject is not its essence. [This is] for the existences of the conditions, and it is not so. The commentator will mention in the investigation of refuting infinite regress what will refute this speech.
His statement: "And it [i.e., that collection] requires a subject specific to it." It was objected to him: If it were established that that collection requires a subject specific to the assumed first event in one of the ways mentioned in the Eastern investigations, their purpose would be achieved without need for the other premises, and the argument would also not be by dispositional potentiality. The answer: That the establishment of the subject for the collection in one of the mentioned ways is only through the other premises that include the argument by dispositional potentiality; for what is established without them is that it has a subject, but as for that subject being existent in such-and-such a way, it is through the other premises; so reflect.
His statement: "like its relation to another" — there is a denial; because those successive things, on the supposition of granting their permissibility and necessity, may be things subsisting by themselves, suitable for the event according to their essences in varying degrees.
His statement: "i.e., for that subject there are dispositions" — if you say: Why was not consideration given to the agent side of dispositional potentiality regarding the act and bringing into existence? I say: Because the variation is not in the agency; for the conditions are conditions of the existence of the effect initially, although they may be considered accidentally in relation to the agent.
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage provides the proof that a collection of successive events (e.g., a series of events leading to a temporal thing) must have a specific material subject (mahall). The author argues that without such a subject, the specification of one event over another would be an unjustified preference (tarjih bila murajjih). He then concludes that the subject must have successive dispositions (isti'dadat muta'aqiba), each preceding another ad infinitum. The passage then presents several objections and answers: 1) An objection that the argument assumes that a separate entity relates equally to all things, but the objector says the conditions could have inherent specificity. 2) An objection that once a subject is posited, the event is preceded by matter so no further premises are needed; the answer explains that the subject may be the quiddity of the event itself, so we need to prove that the conditions are existent dispositions requiring an existent subject. 3) An objection that if the necessity of a subject is granted, the argument is complete without needing dispositional potentiality; the answer clarifies that the necessity of a specific existing subject (not just any subject) requires the further premises. 4) An objection that the successive things could be self-subsistent entities suitable to the event; this is denied. 5) An objection asking why not consider dispositional potentiality in the agent; the answer says variation is in the effect, not in the agent's power. The argument thus defends the need for a material subject and successive dispositions.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that once a specific subject is posited, the argument is complete without needing the concept of dispositions.
Correction: The author shows that the subject could be the quiddity, so we must prove that the conditions are existent dispositions, which requires the full argument.

Checkpoint
What is the author's response to the objection that if a subject is established, the event is already preceded by matter?
A) He accepts the objection and modifies the argument.
B) He says the subject might be the quiddity, so further proof is needed.
C) He denies that matter precedes the event.
D) He argues that the subject must be eternal.

Key Takeaway
The proof for a specific subject withstands objections by showing that the conditions must be existent dispositions, not merely quidditative or self-subsistent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The objection argues that once a subject is posited, the conclusion follows immediately. But the response shows that the subject may be the mere essence, not a real existent. In your own life, do you treat spiritual conditions—like sincerity or knowledge—as mere abstract concepts, or do you actively cultivate them as real existent dispositions in your heart? What would change if you treated them as truly existent things that require a prior foundation?
?
The proof insists that conditions vary in intensity and weakness. Consider your faith (iman). Are its conditions—belief, love, fear of Allah—present in you with real intensity, or are they merely theoretical? Which condition is weakest, and what would it mean for you to strengthen it as an existent disposition in your soul?
?
The objections represent different ways to doubt a sound argument. Which of these five objections do you find yourself most tempted to make when confronted with a theological truth that challenges your comfort? Does that objection reveal a lack of trust in the reasoning, or a deeper resistance to submitting to the truth? How will you respond to that resistance today?

Dispositional Potentiality: Definition and Proof of Its Reality
Defines al-imkan al-isti'dadi and argues for its existence via gradation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand what dispositional potentiality (al-imkan al-isti'dadi) is and why kalam scholars argued it is an existing attribute with real gradation, not a mere mental concept.

Core Idea
Gradation proves reality: what truly is can be more or less.

In this passage, the author defines dispositional potentiality as a quality that admits degrees of proximity, distance, strength, and weakness. He then argues that such variation proves it is an existing thing, because pure non-existence cannot vary. Finally, he notes that this entire reasoning rests on a rejection of the free divine agent, setting up a critique to come.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage once to get a feel for its structure and key terms. Notice the technical terms like 'الإمكان الاستعدادي' and 'استعداد'.
2
Identify the definition
Locate where the author defines what dispositional potentiality is. It is described as a 'disposition' that brings the eternal cause closer to producing a specific effect.
3
Follow the argument from variation
The author proves that this disposition is an existing thing by pointing out that it varies in proximity/distance and strength/weakness. He gives the example of a sperm vs. elements. Understand why such variation cannot occur in pure non-existence.
This is the key proof: gradation implies reality.
4
Notice the critique
At the end, the author states that this entire argument is based on a false principle: the denial of a free agent and the assertion of necessary causation. This is a critical point for later refutation.
Understand that the definition is not accepted as is by the author; it is presented as the view of opponents.
5
Reflect on the broader debate
Consider how this concept fits into the larger kalam discourse on causality and divine attributes. Why would the author mention the false principle?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن كانا بحيث لا يجتمعان معاً في الوجود، ( ومقرب للعلة الموجدة ) القديمة (إلى المعلول ( المعين ( بعد بعدها عنه، ومقرب لذلك المعلول إلى الوجود، ومبعد له عن العدم. فإن المعلول الحادث إذا توقف على ما لا يتناهى من الحوادث المتعاقبة السابقة عليه فخروج كل واحد منها إلى الوجود يقرب الفاعل القديم إلى التأثير في ذلك الحادث تقريباً متدرجاً، حتى تصل النوبة إليه فيوجد. (وهو) أي هذا الاستعداد الحاصل لمحل ذلك الحادث هو ( هو المسمى بالإمكان الاستعدادي) لذلك الحادث، ( وإنه أمر موجود لتفاوته بالقرب والبعد ) ، والقوة والضعف . ( فإن استعداد النطفة للإنسان أقرب وأقوى من استعداد العناصر له، ولا يتصور التفاوت في القرب والبعد والقوة والضعف في العدم الصرف ( والنفي المحض). فإذن هو أمر وجودي، ومحله ( الموجود أيضا هو المادة. وهذا ( الاستدلال الذي هو بالإمكان الاستعدادي مبني على أصلهم الفاسد، وهو نفي القادر المختار)، والقول بالإيجاب؛
And they are such that they cannot coexist in existence, (and they bring the eternal efficient cause) closer to the specific effect (after its distance from it, and they bring that effect closer to existence, and distance it from non-existence. For if the temporal effect depends on an infinite series of successive preceding events, then the emergence of each one of them into existence gradually brings the eternal agent closer to influencing that event, until the turn reaches it and it comes into existence. (And it), i.e., this disposition obtained for the subject of that event, is (what is called dispositional potentiality) for that event, (and it is an existing thing because of its variation in proximity and distance, and strength and weakness. (For the disposition of the sperm for [becoming] a human is nearer and stronger than the disposition of the elements for it, and variation in proximity and distance and strength and weakness is inconceivable in pure non-existence (and absolute negation). So it is an existential thing, and its subject (also existing) is matter. And this (argument which is by dispositional potentiality is based on their false principle, which is the negation of the powerful free agent), and the assertion of necessitation.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage defines and proves the concept of al-imkan al-isti'dadi (dispositional potentiality). It begins by describing the function of successive events: they bring the eternal cause closer to producing a specific effect in a gradual manner, and they bring the effect closer to existence and further from non-existence. The disposition (isti'dad) that results in the subject of the event is called 'dispositional potentiality'. The author then proves that this disposition is an existing thing (amr mawjud) because it admits of variation (tafawut) in proximity/distance and strength/weakness. For example, the disposition of a sperm to become a human is closer and stronger than the disposition of the elements to become a human. Such gradation cannot exist in pure non-existence. Therefore, it must be an existential attribute, and its subject is matter. Finally, the author notes that this whole argument is built on a false principle: the negation of the free agent (nafy al-qadir al-mukhtar) and the doctrine of necessitation (al-qawl bil-ijab). This critique sets up the refutation in later discussions.

Correction: The author argues that it is an existing attribute because it admits of real gradation (proximity/distance, strength/weakness), which cannot occur in pure non-existence.

Checkpoint
What evidence does the author provide to show that dispositional potentiality (al-imkan al-isti'dadi) is an existing thing?
A) It is mentioned in the Quran.
B) It admits of variation in strength and weakness, which cannot occur in non-existence.
C) It is created directly by God.
D) It is a necessary attribute of all substances.

Key Takeaway
Dispositional potentiality is proven to be an existing attribute because it admits of degrees, which pure non-existence cannot.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Your own spiritual state – is it closer to the strong disposition of sperm towards life, or the weak disposition of elements? What does the degree of your eagerness for good deeds and your distance from sin say about the reality of your faith? Will you today take one concrete step to increase your 'nearness' to obedience?
?
The argument in this lesson is built on denying that God acts by free choice. Do you sometimes rely on your own 'disposition' or 'potential' as if it were automatic, forgetting that your existence and every good in it depends directly on the free will of al-Qadir al-Mukhtar? Pause and recognise one area where you have acted as though you were self-sufficient. Will you repent and reaffirm your dependence on Him?
?
If the kind of potentiality described here were real, it would be a quality that varies. How is your own potential to know and worship God growing or shrinking right now? Are you actively strengthening your isti'dad through study, dhikr, and action, or are you letting it weaken? What will you do about it today?

Definition and Proof of Dispositional Possibility
Al-Iji defines al-imkan al-isti'dadi and proves it is existent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of dispositional possibility (al-imkan al-isti'dadi) and the rational proof that it is an existent reality, not a mere mental construct.

Core Idea
Dispositional possibility is an existing quality because it admits degrees, which pure non-existence cannot.

Al-Iji begins by describing the scenario where an eternal cause gradually influences a temporal effect through a chain of events. The preparedness that arises in the material substrate is termed dispositional possibility. This passage then provides a concise proof that this preparedness is an existent attribute, grounded in the observable fact that it varies in intensity. Read on to see how the argument unfolds.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without detailed analysis, then read the literal translation. Let the overall flow of the argument settle in your mind.
Notice the step-by-step reasoning: scenario, definition, then proof.
2
Identify the two main parts
The passage has a definition section (beginning to 'dispositional possibility') and a proof section (from 'it is an existent thing' onward). Separate them mentally.
The proof relies on the impossibility of gradation in pure non-existence.
3
Reflect on the proof logic
Ask yourself: Why does the fact that preparedness can be 'nearer and stronger' or 'remoter and weaker' prove it must be an existing thing?
Pure non-existence has no degrees—something either exists or not. Gradation requires existence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن كانا بحيث لا يجتمعان معاً في الوجود، ( ومقرب للعلة الموجدة ) القديمة (إلى المعلول ( المعين ( بعد بعدها عنه، ومقرب لذلك المعلول إلى الوجود، ومبعد له عن العدم. فإن المعلول الحادث إذا توقف على ما لا يتناهى من الحوادث المتعاقبة السابقة عليه فخروج كل واحد منها إلى الوجود يقرب الفاعل القديم إلى التأثير في ذلك الحادث تقريباً متدرجاً، حتى تصل النوبة إليه فيوجد. (وهو) أي هذا الاستعداد الحاصل لمحل ذلك الحادث هو ( هو المسمى بالإمكان الاستعدادي) لذلك الحادث، ( وإنه أمر موجود لتفاوته بالقرب والبعد ) ، والقوة والضعف . ( فإن استعداد النطفة للإنسان أقرب وأقوى من استعداد العناصر له، ولا يتصور التفاوت في القرب والبعد والقوة والضعف في العدم الصرف ( والنفي المحض). فإذن هو أمر وجودي، ومحله ( الموجود أيضا هو المادة.
And if they are such that they do not coexist in existence, and they bring the eternal efficient cause nearer to the specific effect after its remoteness from it, and bring that effect nearer to existence and remove it from non-existence. For if the originated effect depends on an infinite series of successive originated events preceding it, then the emergence of each one into existence gradually brings the eternal agent nearer to effecting that event, until the turn reaches it and it comes into existence. And this preparedness acquired by the locus of that event is what is called 'dispositional possibility' for that event, and it is an existent thing because it differs in nearness and remoteness, and strength and weakness. For the preparedness of the sperm for a human is nearer and stronger than the preparedness of the elements for it, and difference in nearness and remoteness and strength and weakness cannot be conceived in pure non-existence and absolute negation. Therefore it is an existent thing, and its locus is also existent, namely matter.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage, from the matn of the Mawaqif, defines al-imkan al-isti'dadi (dispositional possibility) and provides a proof that it is an existent reality. The passage begins by describing a scenario where two things cannot coexist in existence, but through a series of successive originated events, the eternal cause is gradually brought nearer to producing a specific effect. The preparedness that arises in the locus of that event is called al-imkan al-isti'dadi. The proof that this preparedness is existent is that it admits variation in nearness/remoteness and strength/weakness; for example, the preparedness of a sperm for becoming a human is nearer and stronger than the preparedness of the elements. Such variation cannot be attributed to pure non-existence or absolute negation, which have no degrees. Therefore, since it admits gradation, it must be an existent thing, and its locus must also be existent, which is matter. The argument follows the philosophers' assumption that the cause is eternal and the effect depends on a chain of events.

Misconception: Dispositional possibility is just a mental concept or a mere logical possibility.
Correction: The passage argues that because it admits degrees (stronger/weaker), it cannot be a mere mental concept; it must be an existing quality in the material substrate.

Checkpoint

B) Because it admits variation in strength and weakness.
C) Because it is the locus of accidents.
D) Because it is a mental concept.

Key Takeaway
Dispositional possibility is an existent quality in matter that admits degree and is required for the gradual becoming of effects.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

What concrete step will you take today to move from 'elements' level to 'sperm' level in your sincerity or devotion?
?
The passage says the eternal cause is gradually brought nearer to the effect through successive events. How does this principle of gradual nearness apply to your journey toward Allah? Are you relying on a sudden transformation, or are you appreciating the value of each small step that brings you closer? What is the next 'event' in your series that you will actualize?

Precedence as an Additional Existent
Commentator explains that precedence is an additional existent attribute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the commentator's reasoning that temporal precedence is an additional attribute that exists externally, distinct from existence and non-existence.

Core Idea
Precedence is a real, additional attribute, not just a relative notion.

In this passage, the commentator defends the claim that precedence (al-taqaddum) is an additional, externally real attribute. He addresses possible misconceptions and shows why precedence must be more than the mere existence or non-existence of the thing. This lesson walks through the logical steps of his argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice how the commentator responds to specific phrases from the original text.
2
Identify the main claim
Identify that the passage argues precedence is an additional existent, not identical to existence or non-existence.
The core claim is that precedence is a real attribute.
3
Follow the objections and replies
The commentator addresses three points: why precedence isn't existence, why it isn't a part, and why it isn't privative. Follow each argument carefully.
4
Consider the conclusion about substrate
Understand why precedence requires an actually existing substrate, not non-existence.
This final point ties the proof together.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( ويستحيل إلخ) وإلا لكان الشيء موجوداً ومعدوماً معاً؛ لأن الصفة الثبوتية تقتضي وجود الموصوف . قوله : (أمر زائد إلخ) إذ لا يجوز أن يكون جزءاً لأن النسبة يمتنع أن تكون جزءاً لأحد الطرفين، وإلا لزم أن تكون متقدمة ومتأخرة، ولذا لم يتعرض لنفيه . قوله لصدقه على الممتنعات وما من شأنه الوجود في الخارج لا يمكن اتصاف المعدوم به كما مر غير مرة . فاندفع ما قيل : إنه لا يدل على كونه عدمياً إلا إذا ثبت أنه لا يصدق إلا على الممتنعات وهو ممنوع. قوله: (من محل) فيمتنع أن يكون محله عدم الحادث، ومن هذا ظهر وجه التعرض لوجود المحل في الاستدلال ومنع وجوديته في الجواب .
His statement: (And it is impossible, etc.) Otherwise the thing would be both existent and non‑existent together; because a positive attribute necessitates the existence of the described. His statement: (An additional thing, etc.) Since it cannot be a part because a relation cannot be a part of one of the two relata, otherwise it would be both prior and posterior; and that is why he did not address its negation. His statement: (Because it is true of impossibles) And whatever has the quality of existence in the external cannot be attributed to the non‑existent, as has been stated many times. So what was said is refuted: that it does not indicate its being privative unless it is established that it is only true of impossibles, which is denied. His statement: (From a substrate) So it is impossible for its substrate to be the non‑existence of the originated thing; and from this the reason for addressing the existence of the substrate in the proof and the denial of its existentiality in the answer becomes clear.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This is a commentary passage that explains and defends the proof that precedence (التقدم) is something additional to existence and non‑existence and exists externally. The commentator first explains the original text's statement that it is impossible for precedence to be the existence of the thing (otherwise the thing would simultaneously be existent and non‑existent, because a positive attribute requires an existent subject). Next, he clarifies that precedence cannot be a part of the thing, because a relation cannot be a constituent of one of its relata. Then he addresses an objection: if precedence were only true of impossible non‑existents, it would be privative; but the commentator responds that it is also predicated of temporal existents, so it must be positive. Finally, he shows that precedence requires a substrate, and that substrate cannot be non‑existence; thus the existence of the substrate is proven in the argument, even though the opponent denies its existentiality in the answer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Precedence is just a relative concept with no real existence.
Correction: The commentator argues that precedence is an additional attribute that exists externally, not just a relation.

Checkpoint
Why does the commentator argue that precedence cannot be the existence of the thing?
A) Because existence is not a relational concept.
B) Because that would make the thing both existent and non‑existent at once.
C) Because precedence is an illusion.
D) Because existence is a part of the thing.

Key Takeaway
Temporal precedence is a real, additional attribute that exists externally, not reducible to existence or non-existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

What would it mean to treat Allah's attributes as equally real even when they surpass your imagination?
?
The commentator argues that if precedence were just the existence itself, it would lead to contradiction. Where in your faith do you need to accept that some matters require careful reasoning rather than oversimplification?
?
The passage defends that precedence is not merely a privative concept. Are there areas in your spiritual life where you view God's actions or attributes as mere privations (absences) rather than positive acts of will? How can you shift to seeing God's governance as actively positive in every moment?

Objection and Answer on Precedence as Qualified Non‑Existence
Objection that precedence is non‑existence described as prior, and its refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why defining precedence as non‑existence qualified by prior connection is circular and fails to solve the problem.

Core Idea
Precedence cannot be reduced to a description of non‑existence without circularity.

In this passage, the commentator addresses a subtle objection: perhaps precedence can be defined as mere non‑existence that is described as being connected to existence in a prior way. This seems to avoid making precedence a positive attribute. But the commentator shows that the description itself smuggles in the very concept we are trying to define, making the argument circular.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice how the objector proposes that precedence could be non‑existence with a specific qualification.
The objection tries to preserve non‑existence while adding a relational description.
2
Understand the rejection of absolute or posterior connection
The commentator says that mere connection (without direction) or connection as posterior does not capture precedence. Only connection as prior would work.
This highlights that the direction of connection matters.
3
Grasp the circularity argument
Connection as prior already contains the idea of precedence. Calling it a 'description' does not avoid the problem; it merely renames the same concept, so the objection is circular.
This is the key insight: you cannot define a term by using the same term in the definition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( ولا نفس عدمه لأن العدم قبل إلخ) فإن قلت: لم لا يجوز أن يكون التقدم عدماً مأخوذاً بوصف الاتصال بالوجود قبلاً؟ قلت : لأن مطلق الاتصال، وكذا الاتصال بطريق التأخر لا يكفي، والاتصال بطريق القبلية يشتمل على التقدم؛ إذ تغيير العبارة لا يجدي، فننقل الكلام إليه فتأمل.
His statement: (Nor the same as its non‑existence because non‑existence before, etc.) For if you say: Why is it not permissible for precedence to be non‑existence taken with the description of connection to existence as prior? I say: Because absolute connection, and likewise connection as posterior, is insufficient; and connection as prior includes precedence itself; for changing the wording does not avail, so we transfer the discussion to that, so reflect.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and its answer within the broader discussion. The objector suggests that precedence might simply be non‑existence qualified by being connected to existence in a prior manner. The commentator refutes this by noting that absolute connection or posterior connection does not capture precedence; only connection as prior does. But that qualification already contains the concept of precedence, so it is circular—merely renaming the same idea. Thus the objection fails.

Correction: The qualification 'prior' already contains the concept, so the definition is circular and fails.

Checkpoint
What is the main problem with defining precedence as non‑existence qualified as prior?
A) It makes precedence a positive attribute.
B) The qualification itself assumes precedence, leading to circularity.
C) Non‑existence cannot have a qualification.
D) The connection is too vague.

Key Takeaway
Defining precedence as non‑existence qualified by prior connection fails because the qualification itself assumes precedence, making the argument circular.

Is Precedence a Positive Attribute?
Objection that precedence is not positive and the counter-objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between direct inherence and concomitant relation, and how precedence remains a positive attribute of time.

Core Idea
Precedence is positive because it belongs to time, not to non-existence.

In this passage, an objection is raised: 'Precedence cannot be a positive attribute because it attaches to non-existence.' The commentator refines this by distinguishing between direct inherence and concomitant relation. By arguing that precedence's real subject is time, its positive nature is preserved. This brief exchange introduces a key distinction in kalam metaphysics.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the structure of objection and response.
2
Identify the objection
The objector claims precedence is not positive because it occurs to non-existence. Mark the phrase 'نمنع كون التقدم أمراً وجودياً'.
This is the core of the objection.
3
Understand the counter-objection
The commentator says the occurrence to non-existence is not real (عروض حقيقي) but rather a concomitance (مقارنة) with non-existence's real subject, time.
4
Reflect on the implication
Because precedence primarily belongs to time, its attribution to non-existence does not make it privative. The objection's ground fails.
5
Note the postponement
The discussion is postponed to the investigations of time, indicating deeper context later.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( وجوابه : أنا نمنع كون التقدم أمراً وجودياً ، فإنه يعرض للعدم) قيل : عروضه للعدم ليس عروضاً حقيقياً، بل معناه مقارنة العدم لمعروضه الحقيقي، أعني الزمان، وعروضه للعدم بهذا المعنى لا يستلزم عدميته فالسند لا يستلزم المنع وسيأتي لهذا الكلام تتمة في مباحث الزمان إن شاء الله تعالى .
His statement: (And its answer: we deny that precedence is a positive thing, for it occurs to non‑existence.) It was said: Its occurrence to non‑existence is not a real occurrence, but rather its meaning is the concomitance of non‑existence with its real subject, namely time; and its occurrence to non‑existence in this sense does not necessitate its privative status, so the ground does not necessitate the denial; and a completion of this discussion will come in the investigations of time, God willing.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This is an objection and answer again. The objector claims precedence is not positive because it attaches to non‑existence. The commentator, however, refines the objection: even if precedence attaches to non‑existence, that attachment is not direct; it is a concomitance (مقارنة) of non‑existence with its real subject, which is time. Therefore, precedence is not thereby shown to be privative. The discussion is postponed to the section on time.

Key Terms

العدم
العروض

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If a concept applies to non‑existence, it must itself be non‑existent (privative).
Correction: The passage shows that precedence's application to non‑existence is only concomitant; its real subject is time, so it remains a positive attribute.

Checkpoint
Why does the commentator say that precedence's occurrence to non‑existence does not prove it is privative?
A) Because non‑existence cannot have attributes.
B) Because precedence really belongs to time, and only secondarily to non‑existence.
C) Because precedence is an illusion.
D) Because the text says so without explanation.

Key Takeaway
Precedence is a positive attribute because its real subject is time; its association with non-existence is only concomitant.

Rejecting the Imagination's Judgment of Precedence
Refuting the claim that the imagination's judgment of precedence as existent is valid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the imagination's judgment about the existence of precedence is rejected and how the commentator refutes the objection that precedence must have time as an essential substrate.

Core Idea
The imagination errs in abstract matters; precedence is not a real existent.

This passage confronts a common psychological argument: if we intuitively feel that one thing precedes another, that feeling must indicate a real property called 'precedence.' The commentator shows that such intuitive judgments from the imagination are unreliable in metaphysical questions, using examples about God's nature. Then he addresses a more refined objection that concedes the relative nature of precedence but insists on time as a real substrate.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the commentator uses two examples to illustrate the imagination's fallibility.
2
Identify the main argument
The commentator rejects the imagination's judgment that precedence is existent. Find the reasoning: the imagination is not reliable in purely intelligible matters, as shown by examples.
The examples are about God's transcendence and visibility in the Hereafter.
3
Understand the objection
The objector concedes that priority and non-priority are privative but argues that the intellect's judgment that things have such attributes requires an essential substrate, which is time.
This objection is more sophisticated; it accepts the commentator's premise but tries to salvage a real substrate.
4
Follow the commentator's response
The commentator concedes the need for a substrate but denies that it must exist externally. It could be an intellectual concept (أمر عقلي) that serves as substrate for relational judgments.
This is a key move: the substrate can be a mental construct, not a real external entity.
5
Grasp the final clarification
Even if we accept time as the substrate, its external existence is not required for the conclusion that the originated thing is preceded by a duration. That is a separate issue.
The commentator sets aside the question of time's external existence as irrelevant to the main point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( والحاكم بثبوته ) أي بثبوت التقدم في نفسه هو ( الوهم ) ببديهته دون العقل (وحكمه) في المعقولات الصرفة (مردود، كما في تحيز الباري) ، فإن الوهم يحكم ببديهيته أن كل موجود قائم بذاته فهو متحيز ومخصوص بجهة، (و) كما في كون كل مرئي مقابلاً للرائي ( أو في حكمه)، كما في الأمور المشاهدة في المرآة وهذان الحكمان باطلان لأن الباري تعالى ليس بمتحيز أصلاً، وهو مرئي في الدار الآخرة بدون المقابلة وما في حكمها، فكذا حكمه على التقدم بأنه موجود باطل فإن قلت : هب أن القبلية واللاقبلية عدميتان لكن الحكم باتصاف الأشياء بهما حكم صحيح تشهد به بديهة العقل فلا بد لها من معروض ذاتي هو الزمان . قلت : هذا مسلم لكن لا يلزم منه وجود ذلك المعروض في الخارج، بل جاز أن يكون أمراً عقلياً معروضاً في نفس الأمر لما هو اعتباري . . قوله : (هذا) (مسلم أي أنه لا بد له من معروض ذاتي، لكنه لا يلزم منه وجود ذلك المعروض ؛ لجواز أن يكون عدم ذلك الحادث، فلا حكمه بأنه هو الزمان . وبما ذكرنا ظهر اندفاع ما قيل بعد تسليم أن معروضه الذاتي هو الزمان ثبت المطلوب وهو مسبوقية الحادث بالمدة ولا يهمنا بيان كونه موجوداً في الخارج، فإنه مطلوب آخر مذكور في مقامه .
His statement: (And the one who judges it to be established) i.e., the establishment of precedence in itself is (the imagination) by its intuition, not the intellect, (and its judgment) in purely intelligible matters (is rejected, as in the case of the immanence of the Creator), for the imagination judges intuitively that every existing thing subsisting by itself is extended and specific to a direction; (and) as in the case of every visible thing being opposite to the viewer (or in that ruling), like things seen in a mirror; and these two judgments are false because the Creator, exalted, is not extended at all, and He is visible in the Hereafter without opposition and what is similar to it; so likewise its judgment that precedence is existent is false. For if you say: Granted that priority and non‑priority are privative, but the judgment that things are described by them is a correct judgment attested by the intuition of the intellect, so they must have an essential substrate which is time. I say: This is conceded, but it does not necessitate the existence of that substrate in the external; rather, it is possible that it be an intellectual thing that serves as substrate in reality for what is relational. His statement: (This) (is conceded, i.e., it necessarily requires an essential substrate, but the existence of that substrate in the external does not follow; for it is possible that it be the non‑existence of that originated thing, so his judgment that it is time does not follow. And by what we have mentioned, the refutation of what was said becomes clear: that after conceding that its essential substrate is time, the desired result is established, namely that the originated thing is preceded by a duration; and we are not concerned with proving its existence in the external, for that is another desired result mentioned in its place.
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the argument that precedence is existent because the imagination (الوهم) judges it to be so. The commentator points out that the imagination's judgments are not reliable in purely intelligible matters, giving two examples: the imagination thinks every self‑subsistent being must be extended and located in a direction (like bodies), but God is not extended; also, it thinks every visible thing must be opposite the viewer, but in a mirror things are seen without direct opposition. Similarly, the imagination's judgment that precedence is existent is false. The objector then concedes that priority and non‑priority might be privative but insists that the intellect judges that things have such attributes, so they must have an essential substrate, namely time. The commentator responds that this substrate does not have to be externally existent; it could be an intellectual concept (أمر عقلي) that underlies the relational judgment. In the final note, the commentator clarifies that even if we accept time as the substrate, the existence of time in the external is not required for the desired conclusion—that the originated thing is preceded by a duration—which is another topic.

العقل
تحيز الباري
المقابلة
الزمان
المعروض الذاتي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any intuitive judgment of the mind is reliable, including those of the imagination.
Correction: The commentator shows that the imagination often errs in metaphysical matters (e.g., thinking God must be extended, or that visibility requires opposition). Hence its judgment about precedence is not trustworthy.

Checkpoint
Why does the commentator reject the imagination's judgment that precedence is existent?
A) Because the imagination is always wrong.
B) Because the imagination makes false claims about God's transcendence and visibility, showing its fallibility.
C) Because precedence is not a real concept.
D) Because the intellect never agrees with the imagination.

Key Takeaway
The imagination's judgment about precedence is not reliable; precedence is a relative notion, and its substrate (time) need not be an external existent.

How Plurality Can Be Described as Having Unity
Commentator answers the objection that the many cannot have unity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the commentator resolves the apparent contradiction between the plurality of the many and its being described as having unity, by distinguishing between different aspects of consideration.

Core Idea
Plurality and unity can coexist in the same essence when considered from different aspects.

In this passage, the commentator addresses a critical objection: if unity and plurality are opposites, how can something that is many also be described as one? The answer lies in a subtle distinction between considering the essence of the many in detail (as the subject of plurality) and in summary (as the subject of unity). This lesson unpacks the objection and its resolution, which is a key tool in kalam for reconciling seemingly contradictory attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the objection presented by the hypothetical questioner. Understand why someone would object that if unity accompanies existence, then the many should also be a unity.
The objection is based on the idea that if unity is co-extensive with existence, then everything that exists should be a unity, including the many.
2
Identify the two answers
The commentator gives two formulations of the same answer: one based on 'observation of the attribute' of plurality, and another based on the distinction between 'detail' and 'summary'. Notice how they both resolve the objection.
Both formulations rely on changing the aspect under which the essence is considered.
3
Reflect on the deeper point
Consider why this resolution is valid: the conjunction of opposites is only impossible when they apply to the same subject under the same aspect. Here, the aspects differ (detail vs. summary, or with vs. without observation of plurality).
This principle is widely used in kalam to reconcile divine attributes that might otherwise seem contradictory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرصد الرابع - المقصد الأول : الوحدة تساوق الوجود
أحد المتقابلين للآخر، إنما المحال عروضه لمعروض الآخر، فالعشرية عارضة للجسم مثلاً، والوحدة عارضة للعشرية، فلم يتحدا في الموضوع حتى يكون ذلك مانعاً من تقابلهما . فإن قلت : فعلى هذا لا يصح أن كل ما له أن كل ما هو موجود وحدة، فإن الكثير موجود ولم يعرض له ،وحدة كما اعترفتم به :قلت المراد من عروض الوحدة للكثرة أنها عارضة لذات الكثير، مع ملاحظة صفة الكثرة بخلاف الكثرة؛ فإنها عارضة لتلك الذات بلا ملاحظة كثرة . وبعبارة أخرى ذات الكثير من حيث التفصيل معروضة للكثرة ، ومن حيث الإجمال معروضة للوحدة، ولا استحالة في عروض المتقابلين
كذلك اجتماع المتقابلين بالعرض لأنه يستلزم اجتماع المتقابلين بالذات، فلا يرد أن الوحدة والكثرة ليستا متقابلين بالذات حتى يمتنع اجتماعهما.
قوله: (المراد إلخ) فمعنى قوله : عرض الوحدة للكثرة أن للكثرة مدخلاً في عروضها، حتى لو لم يلاحظ اتصافه بالكثرة لم تعرضه الوحدة. وما قيل: إن اللام في قوله : لم يعرضا لشيء واحد لام الأجل، فيكون مآل قوله : لا للكثرة لا لأجل ذاته فلا حاجة إلى التطويل الذي ذكره الشارح قدس سره، ولا يرد الاعتراض الآتي فوهم محض؛ لأن اختلاف سبب المتقابلين لا يؤثر في جواز اجتماعهما، بل لا بد في ذلك من اختلاف المحل ذاتاً أو اعتباراً.
قوله : ( ملاحظة صفة (الكثرة زاد لفظ : الصفة إشارة إلى أنه لا بد من ملاحظة الكثرة باعتبار كونها صفة قائمة به، فالموصوف ذات الكثير مع الكثرة لا ذات الكثير في نفسه، ولا مقيداً بالكثرة موصوفاً بها، وإلا لزم اجتماع المتقابلين.
قوله: (من حيث التفصيل بأن لم يعتبر اتصافه بمرتبة واحدة من مراتب الكثرة ومن حيث الإجمال بأن يعتبر اتصافه بها، فماله هو الجواب الأول، لا فرق بينهما إلا بالتعبير، وليس المراد بالتفصيل والإجمال أن يدرك ذلك الكثير مفصلاً، وأن يدرك مجملاً، على قياس ما يقال في الفرق بين الحد والمحدود، حتى يرد أن الاختلاف بالتفصيل والإجمال راجع إلى الاختلاف في الإدراك دون ذات المعروض حتى ينفع في عدم لزوم اجتماع المتقابلين كيف ولو أريد ذلك كان جواباً آخر لا الجواب السابق بعبارة أخرى.
قوله : ( المراد من عروض الوحدة للكثرة إلخ لا يخفى أن سياق كلامه على أن اللام صلة العروض، فإراداة هذا المعنى على هذا التقدير إنما يصح بحمل الكلام على المسامحة، واعلم أن هذا الجواب أقرب من الجواب الثاني الذي أشار إليه بقوله : ولنا أن نقول إلخ، ولذا قدمه، وإن كان الجواب الثاني الصق بعبارة المتن . فعلى الأول يكون معنى قوله : حتى الكثير أن الكثير من حيث هو كثير أي مع ملاحظة صفة الكثرة. وقوله : فإنهما لم يعرضا لشيء واحد أي من جهة واحدة. وقوله : عرض الوحدة للكثرة أو الوحدة تعرض للكثير بملاحظة الكثرة، لا للكثير الذي يلاحظ تفصيله، فيكون المآل إلى حيثية الإجمال والتفصيل وأما على الثاني فالأمر ظاهر.
The fourth observatory - The first purpose: Unity accompanies existence. One of the two opposites to the other; only impossible is its occurrence to the subject of the other. For example, 'ten-ness' occurs to the body, and unity occurs to the ten-ness, so they do not unite in the subject such that this would prevent their contrast. For you say: On this basis, it is not correct that everything that has... that every existent is a unity, for the many exists and unity does not occur to it, as you have admitted. I say: The meaning of the occurrence of unity to plurality is that it occurs to the essence of the many, with the observation of the attribute of plurality, unlike plurality; for it occurs to that essence without observation of plurality. In other words, the essence of the many from the aspect of detail is the subject of plurality, and from the aspect of summary is the subject of unity, and there is no impossibility in the occurrence of the two opposites. Likewise, the conjunction of opposites accidentally is impossible because it necessitates the conjunction of opposites essentially, so it is not objected that unity and plurality are not opposites in essence such that their conjunction would be impossible. His statement: (The meaning etc.) So the meaning of his statement: 'the occurrence of unity to plurality' is that plurality has a role in its occurrence, so that if his being characterized by plurality were not observed, unity would not occur to him. And what was said: that the lam in his statement 'they do not occur to one thing' is the lam of purpose, so the import of his statement would be 'not for the sake of plurality' i.e., not for the sake of its essence, so there is no need for the lengthy discussion mentioned by the commentator (may his secret be sanctified), and the following objection does not arise, it is sheer illusion; because the difference of the cause of the two opposites does not affect the permissibility of their conjunction; rather, what is required for that is difference of the subject intrinsically or consideratively. His statement: (Observation of the attribute of plurality) he added the word 'attribute' to indicate that it is necessary to observe plurality as being an attribute subsisting in him, so the described is the essence of the many together with plurality, not the essence of the many in itself, nor restricted by plurality as described by it, otherwise the conjunction of opposites would follow. His statement: (From the aspect of detail is that his being characterized by one level of the levels of plurality is not considered, and from the aspect of summary is that his being characterized by it is considered) so what he has is the first answer; there is no difference between them except in expression. And the intent by 'detail' and 'summary' is not that that many is perceived in detail and perceived in summary, on the analogy of what is said about the difference between the definition and the defined, such that it would be objected that the difference by detail and summary goes back to the difference in perception not to the essence of the subject, so that it would be useful in preventing the necessary conjunction of opposites. How so? For if that were intended, it would be another answer, not the previous answer in other words. His statement: (The meaning of the occurrence of unity to plurality etc.) It is not hidden that the flow of his statement is that the lam is for relation of occurrence, so intending this meaning on this estimation is only valid by carrying the speech on leniency. And know that this answer is closer than the second answer which he indicated by his statement 'and we may say etc.', hence he gave it priority, even though the second answer is more sticking to the text of the matn. On the first, the meaning of his statement 'even the many' is that the many insofar as it is many, i.e., with the observation of the attribute of plurality. And his statement 'for they do not occur to one thing' means from one aspect. And his statement 'the occurrence of unity to plurality' or 'unity occurs to the many by observing plurality, not to the many whose detail is observed', so the import goes to the respect of summary and detail. As for the second, the matter is clear.
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer followed by a detailed commentary on the resolution. The objection is that if unity and plurality are opposites, then how can the many, which is plural, be described as having unity? The answer is that unity occurs to the essence of the many when the attribute of plurality is observed, whereas plurality occurs to the same essence without such observation. This is further explained using the distinction between detailed consideration (tahlil) and summary consideration (ijmal): the essence considered in detail is the subject of plurality, while considered summarily it is the subject of unity. The commentator then clarifies that the conjunction of opposites accidentally would imply essential conjunction, which is impossible, but here the two opposites do not meet in the same subject under the same aspect. He also addresses an alternative interpretation of the preposition 'lam' and critiques it, affirming that the correct understanding requires a difference in the subject either intrinsically (dhat) or consideratively (i'tibar). Finally, he contrasts two answers: the first (based on observation of the attribute) is closer to the truth, while the second (based on lam al-ajal) is more literal to the text.

Key Terms
المتقابلان
العرض
الذات
الاعتبار
التفصيل والإجمال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The distinction between 'detail' and 'summary' is merely about how we perceive the many, not about the essence itself.
Correction: The commentator explicitly states that the difference is in the subject (the essence) itself, not in perception: the essence in detail is the subject of plurality, and in summary it is the subject of unity.

Checkpoint
How does the commentator resolve the objection that the many cannot have unity?
A) By stating that the many has no unity at all.
B) By distinguishing between the essence of the many considered in detail (subject of plurality) and considered summarily (subject of unity).
C) By claiming that unity and plurality are not opposites.
D) By reinterpreting the word 'unity' to mean something else.

Key Takeaway
The many can be described as one because unity and plurality apply to the same essence under different aspects of consideration.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You are a mix of virtues and vices—are you willing to see them as different aspects of the same soul, or do you deny one side to feel consistent? How does this lesson force you to hold both before Allah without self-deception?
?
When you face a contradiction in your understanding of Allah's attributes (e.g., His mercy and justice), do you quickly reject one to resolve the tension? What does this lesson demand you do instead?
?
Consider a time you saw yourself as 'one thing' (e.g., patient) and then acted impatiently. Did you take that as a lie about yourself, or as a different aspect of your essence? How can embracing this distinction transform your repentance?
